(TA.) One says, <foreign lang="ar">مَا أَقَامَ</foreign>

(Ksh.) The saying (Mgh, O, TA) of the Prophet, (O,) related in a trad., (O, TA,) <foreign lang="ar">قَسَمَ غَنَائِمَ خَيْبَرَ عَنْ فُوَاقٍ</foreign>, (Mgh,) or <foreign lang="ar">الغَنَائِمَ يَوْمَ بَدْرٍ عَنْ <ref cref="n34859-3" target="فَوَاقٍ" n="3" type="5" subtype="FSO" lang="ar"/>قَسَمَ</foreign> (O, TA) and <foreign lang="ar">فُوَاقٍ</foreign>, (TA,) means <assumedtropical>(assumed tropical:)</assumedtropical>  <hi rend="ital">He divided the spoils</hi> [<hi rend="ital">of Kheyber,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">on the day of Bedr,</hi>] <hi rend="ital">in the space of the rest between two milkings</hi> of a she-camel: (TA:) or <hi rend="ital">quickly;</hi> (Mgh, O;) <foreign lang="ar">عن فواق</foreign> meaning <foreign lang="ar">صَادِرًا عَنْ</foreign>

                  <hi rend="ital">with a dividing proceeding from quickness</hi>]: (Mgh, O: *) or, as some say, the meaning is, <hi rend="ital">making some</hi> of them [i. e. of those who composed his army] <hi rend="ital">to be more highly distinguished</hi> (

                     <itype>1</itype>        
                     <orth orig="" extent="full" lang="ar">فَاقَهُمْ</orth>
                     <orth extent="full" lang="ar">ذ</orth>
                  </form>, (S, Mgh, O, Msb, K,) derived from <foreign lang="ar">فَوْق</foreign> as signifying the contr. of <foreign lang="ar">تَحْت</foreign>, Mgh.) aor. <foreign lang="ar">يَفُوقُهُمْ</foreign>, (S, O.) inf. n. <foreign lang="ar">فَوْقٌ</foreign> (O, K) and <foreign lang="ar">فَوَاقٌ</foreign> (K) and <foreign lang="ar">فَوْقَانٌ</foreign>, (CK.) <hi rend="ital">He</hi> (a man, S, O, Msb) <hi rend="ital">was,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">became, above them,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">superior to them,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">excelled them,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">surpassed them,</hi> (S, Mgh, O, Msb, K,) namely, his companions, (S, O, Msb, K,) or others (Mgh) in eminence, or <hi rend="ital">dignity,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">nobility.</hi> (S, O, K;) and <hi rend="ital">he overcame them;</hi> (Msb, TA:) and <hi rend="ital">did so in,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">by, an argument</hi> <foreign lang="ar">فُقْتُ فُلَانًا</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">I became better than such a one,</hi> and <hi rend="ital">higher,</hi> and <hi rend="ital">more eminent</hi> or <hi rend="ital">noble;</hi> as though above him in station.(TA.) And <foreign lang="ar">فَاقَتِ الجَارِيَةُ بِالجَمَالِ</foreign>

                  <foreign lang="ar">تَحْت</foreign>; (S, Mgh, O, Msb, K;) [primarily signifying The <hi rend="ital">location that is above,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">over;</hi>] and is an adv. n. (Mgh, Msb, K) of place; (Mgh, Msb;) and a simple noun, indecl., [with dammeh for its termination, when the noun to which it should be prefixed is suppressed, and the meaning of this is intended to be understood, but not the word itself;] but when it is prefixed to another noun [which is either expressed or itself (and not merely its meaning) meant to be understood, and when the noun to which it should be prefixed is suppressed and neither this nor its meaning is meant to be understood,] it is declinable. (K. [For the words <foreign lang="ar">يَكُونُ ٱسْمًا وَظَرْفًا مَبْنِىٌّ</foreign>, the reading of the K in the TA and CK, my MS. copy of the K (which I follow in this case) has <foreign lang="ar">يكون ظرفا واسما مبنيّا</foreign>.]) One says, <foreign lang="ar">زَيْدٌ فَوْقَ السَّطْحِ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">Zeyd is above,</hi> or rather <hi rend="ital">upon, the house-top</hi>]. (Mgh, Msb.) And <foreign lang="ar">العِمَامَةُ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">فَوْقَ الرَّأْسِ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">The turban is above,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">upon, the head</hi>]. (Mgh.) And <foreign lang="ar">طَفَا فَوْقَ المَآءِ</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">It floated upon the water.</hi> (S &amp;c. in art. <foreign lang="ar">طفو</foreign>.) Ks has mentioned the saying, <foreign lang="ar">أَفَوْقَ تَنَامُ أَمْ أَسْفَلَ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">Dost thou,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">wilt thou, sleep in the part that is above</hi> of the house &amp;c., <hi rend="ital">or in the part that is below?</hi> i. e., <hi rend="ital">in the upper part,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">in the lower part?</hi>] with fet-h, as suppressing the noun to which <foreign lang="ar">فوق</foreign> is [meant to be understood as] prefixed. (TA.) Lth says that he who uses it as a <foreign lang="ar">صِفَة</foreign> [by which (like other old writers) he means an adv. n. of place] should use the accus. case, as when one says, <foreign lang="ar">عَبْدُ ٱللّٰهِ فَوْقَ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">زَيْدٍ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">'Abd-Allah is above Zeyd</hi>]: but if you make it simply a noun, you use the nom. case, and say, <foreign lang="ar">فَوْقُهُ رَأْسُهُ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">His superior</hi> (meaning <hi rend="ital">upper</hi>) <hi rend="ital">part is his head</hi>]; for in this instance it is the head itself, and you make each to be governed in the nom. case by the other. (TA.) In the saying in the Kur [xvi. 28], <foreign lang="ar">فَخَرَّ عَلَيْهِمُ ٱلسَّقْفُ مِنْ فَوْقِهِمْ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">And the roof fell on them from above them</hi>], the utility of the phrase <foreign lang="ar">من فوقهم</foreign> is hardly apparent, <pb n="2462"/> because <foreign lang="ar">عليهم</foreign> sometimes serves in its stead: but IJ says that <foreign lang="ar">من فوقهم</foreign> may here have a useful office; for <foreign lang="ar">عَلَى</foreign> is sometimes used in relation to deeds [or events] that are difficult, and deemed onerous; [for instance,] you say, <foreign lang="ar">قَدْ سِرْنَا عَشْرًا</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">وَبَقِيَتْ عَلَيْنَا لَيْلَتَانِ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">We have journeyed ten</hi> nights <hi rend="ital">and</hi> the journeys <hi rend="ital">two nights have remained</hi> as though incumbent <hi rend="ital">on us</hi>]; &amp;c.; so that if it were said <foreign lang="ar">فخرّ عليهم السقف</foreign> without the adding <foreign lang="ar">من فوقهم</foreign>, it might be supposed to be like the saying <foreign lang="ar">عَلَيْهِمْ دَارُهُمْ قَدْ خَرِبَتْ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">Their abode had become in a state of ruin</hi> as a punishment <hi rend="ital">upon them</hi>]; but when He [referring to God] says <foreign lang="ar">من</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">فوقهم</foreign>, that meaning which was supposable ceases to be so; and the meaning becomes this, that it [the roof] fell when they were beneath it. (TA.) <foreign lang="ar">إِذْ جَاؤُوكُمْ مِنْ فَوْقِكُمْ وَمِنْ أَسْفَلَ مِنْكُمْ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">When they came to you from above you and from below you</hi>], in the Kur [xxxiii. 10], relates to Benoo- Kureydhah, who came to them from above them; and to Kureysh and Ghatafán, who came from the district of Mekkeh, from below them. (TA.) <foreign lang="ar">وَٱلَّذِينَ ٱتَّقُوا فَوْقَهُمْ يَوْمَ ٱلْقِيَامَةِ</foreign>, in the Kur [ii. 208], means <assumedtropical>(assumed tropical:)</assumedtropical>  [<hi rend="ital">But those who have been careful of their religious duties</hi>] <hi rend="ital">shall be above them in station</hi> [<hi rend="ital">on the day of resurrection</hi>]. (O.) And one says, [agreeably with what has been stated in the first sentence of this paragraph, <foreign lang="ar">أَخَذَهُ مِنْ فَوْقُ</foreign>, and <foreign lang="ar">أَخَذَهُ مِنْ فَوْقٍ</foreign>, [meaning <assumedtropical>(assumed tropical:)</assumedtropical>  <hi rend="ital">He overcame him,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">overpowered him,</hi> and in like manner <foreign lang="ar">أَتَاهُ من</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">فوق</foreign>, as expl. in the Ham p. 128. i. e. <foreign lang="ar">قَهَرَهُ</foreign> namely, his adversary; and so a hawk, his pr? or quarry.
